<body>

<p>
<table border="0" cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0" width="100%">
	<tr>
		<td id="main0" class="auto-style2" style="height: 8905px">
		<h2 style="font-size: 16px;">G<strong>ent's Joey64 Clone Cart - CIC &amp; 
		Save Type Guide</strong></h2>
		<p class="auto-style2">For use with the Joey64 Flasher and N64 Clone 
		Carts</p>
		<h3 style="font-size: 16px;">
		<br />
		<strong>Game Security CIC List:</strong></h3>
		This page categorizes the N64 library by what CIC security chip it 
		uses. The CIC in an N64 cartridge is simply a means of preventing 
		unlicensed games from working on stock N64 systems. In a sense, the CIC 
		is of no concern to the gamer. The N64 system however, requires the CIC 
		in order to start up a game.<br />
&nbsp;<strong><h3 class="auto-style2">Security CIC Overview:</h3>
		</strong>
		<p class="auto-style2">There are 5 known CICs for NTSC and PAL games:</p>
		<ul>
			<li class="auto-style2"><strong>NTSC:</strong></li>
		</ul>
		<ul>
			<li class="auto-style2">
			<strong>CIC-NUS-6101</strong></li>
			<li class="auto-style2"><strong>
			CIC-NUS-6102</strong></li>
			<li class="auto-style2"><strong>
			CIC-NUS-6103</strong></li>
			<li class="auto-style2"><strong>
			CIC-NUS-6105</strong></li>
			<li class="auto-style2"><strong>
			CIC-NUS-6106</strong></li>
		</ul>
		<ul>
			<li class="auto-style2"><strong>PAL:</strong></li>
		</ul>
		<ul>
			<li class="auto-style2"><strong>
			CIC-NUS-7101</strong></li>
			<li class="auto-style2">
			<strong>CIC-NUS-7102</strong></li>
			<li class="auto-style2"><strong>
			CIC-NUS-7103</strong></li>
			<li class="auto-style2"><strong>
			CIC-NUS-7105</strong></li>
			<li class="auto-style2"><strong>
			CIC-NUS-7106</strong></li>
		</ul>
		<p class="auto-style2">The CIC-6102 chip is considered the standard NTSC security chip. For 
		PAL games it is the CIC-7101. The vast majority of releases use these 
		two CICs,</p>
		so they won't be specifically listed here, for it would be a 
		list of over 250 games.<p class="auto-style2">If a game is not on the below lists, it uses 
		either CIC-6102 if it's NTSC or CIC-7101 for PAL. </p>
		<p class="auto-style2">&nbsp;</p>
		<strong>
		<h3 class="auto-style2">
		CIC-NUS-6101 (NTSC) /
		<strong>
		CIC-NUS-7102 (PAL)
		<font size="4">4K EEPROM</font></strong></h3>
		<p style="font-family: verdana;"><span class="auto-style2">For Joey64 
		Clone Cart Flasher: </span>
		</strong>
		<span class="auto-style2">There is no point as only one game used this.</span></p>
		<ul>
			<li class="auto-style2">Star Fox 64 (<a name="4Kbit_EEPROM0">4Kbit EEPROM</a>)</li>
			<li class="auto-style2">Lylat Wars (Star Fox 64) EUR (<a name="4Kbit_EEPROM1">4Kbit EEPROM</a>)</li>
		</ul>
		<span class="auto-style2">You can howerver use:
		<a href="https://github.com/TheGent/Gents-N64-xdelta-Patches/tree/main/CIC%20Change" target="_blank">
		<strong>Gents-N64-xdelta-Patches CIC Change to 6102/7101</strong></a> 
		for use with the mentioned save type on 6102/7101 </span>
		<p class="auto-style2">&nbsp;</p>
		<h3 class="auto-style2">
		<strong>
		CIC-NUS-610</strong>2 (NTSC) /
		<strong>
		CIC-NUS-710</strong>1 (PAL) <font size="4">4K EEPROM</font></h3>
		<p class="auto-style2">
		For Joey64 Clone Cart Flasher: Use <strong>Mario Party 2</strong> (Clone Cart)<strong> </strong>
		(<strong>256 MBit / 32 MB</strong>)<strong> </strong>for <strong>
		<em>EEPROM (4 Kbits) </em></strong>Save Type</p>
		<p class="auto-style2">This was the most commonly used CIC</p>
		<p class="auto-style2">&nbsp;</p>
		<p>

		<h3 class="auto-style2">
		&nbsp;</h3>
		<h3 class="auto-style2">
		CIC-NUS-6102 (NTSC) /
		CIC-NUS-7101 (PAL) <strong>NO Cartridge </strong>Save</h3>
		<p class="auto-style2">
		For Joey64 Clone Cart Flasher: Use <strong>Mario Party 2</strong> (Clone Cart)<strong> </strong>
		(<strong>256 MBit / 32 MB</strong>)<strong> </strong>for <strong>
		<em>EEPROM (4 Kbits) </em></strong>Save Type</p>
		<p class="auto-style2">This will use the Controller pak or just Password 
		method.&nbsp;</p>
		<p class="auto-style2">&nbsp;</p>

				<td align="center" sdnum="2057;0;0" sdval="256" style="border-top: 1px solid #000000; border-bottom: 1px solid #000000; border-left: 1px solid #000000; border-right: 1px solid #000000" valign="top">
				256</td>
			</tr>
		</table>
		<p class="auto-style2">&nbsp;</p>
		<strong>
		<h3 class="auto-style2">
		CIC-NUS-6106 (NTSC) /
		<strong>
		CIC-NUS-7106 (PAL)

              <table width="100%" border="0" cellspacing="0" cellpadding="0">


  <tr>
          <td style="height: 40px" class="auto-style2">
		  <h3><strong>Game Save Method List:</strong></h3>
		  <p>&nbsp;</p>
		  </td>
          </tr>
          
                  
<p><span class="auto-style2">This page categorizes the N64 library by what method each game uses to save progress. Unlike most game consoles before it, the N64 has many ways of saving, mostly on a technical level. 
			</span>
         
         
<strong></p>
			<h3 style="font-family:verdana;">&nbsp;</h3>
			<h3 style="font-family:verdana;">Save Method Overview</h3></strong>


<p class="auto-style2">These are the 5 known saving methods:</p>

<ul>
<li class="auto-style2">Controller Pak (32,768 bytes) </li>
<li class="auto-style2">EEPROM 4Kilobits (512 bytes)</li>
<li class="auto-style2">EEPROM 16 Kilobits (2048 bytes)</li>
<li class="auto-style2">SRAM 256 Kilobits (32,768 bytes)</li>
<li class="auto-style2">FlashRAM 1024 Kilobits (131,072 
bytes)</li>
<li class="auto-style2">No Save (included at the bottom)</li>
</ul>

<p class="auto-style2">The bottom four methods are for on-cartridge saving. They function basically the same to the end user. SRAM (Static RAM) uses a coin cell battery as it is a volatile form of memory. EEPROM and FlashRAM do not require an external power source to retain data.</p>

<p class="auto-style2">There also exists one unique N64 game, Dezaemon 3D. It uses 768Kbit SRAM, thus also uses a battery. </p>

<p class="auto-style2">NOTE: Sometimes a game uses both on-cart memory and the controller pak. Such games will be placed in each of the relevant lists.</p>
			<p class="auto-style2">&nbsp;</p>

<strong><h3 style="font-family:verdana;"><a name="Controller_Pak">Controller Pak</a></h3></strong>
<p class="auto-style2">Also known as a memory card. Most 3rd party games used this to save. N64 memory cards use a battery. Within about 20 to 25 years from manufacture, their batteries will have to be replaced. </p>

<strong> <h3 style="font-family:verdana;"><a name="4Kbit_EEPROM">4Kbit EEPROM</a></h3></strong>

<strong><h3 style="font-family:verdana;"><a name="16Kbit_EEPROM">16Kbit EEPROM</a></h3></strong>

<p class="auto-style2">As you can see, not many carts used this to save.</p>

<ul>
<li class="auto-style2">Banjo-Tooie</li>
<li class="auto-style2">Conker's Bad Fur Day</li>
<li class="auto-style2">Cruis'n World</li>
<li class="auto-style2">Donkey Kong 64</li>
<li class="auto-style2">Excitebike 64</li>
<li class="auto-style2">Kobe Bryant in NBA Courtside</li>
<li class="auto-style2">Mario Party 3</li>
<li class="auto-style2">Mario Tennis</li>
<li class="auto-style2">Perfect Dark</li>
<li class="auto-style2">Ridge Racer 64</li>
<li class="auto-style2">Star Wars Episode 1 Racer</li>
<li class="auto-style2">Yoshi's Story</li>
</ul>

<strong><h3 style="font-family:verdana;">256Kbit <a name="SRAM">SRAM</a></h3></strong>

<p class="auto-style2">These carts have a battery to power the SRAM when not being played. Like the Controller Pak, these games will eventually need to have their batteries replaced.</p>

<ul>
<li class="auto-style2">1080 Snowboarding</li>
<li class="auto-style2">Dezaemon 3D (JPN, 768Kbit)</li>
<li class="auto-style2">F-Zero X</li>
<li class="auto-style2">Harvest Moon 64</li>
<li class="auto-style2">Legend of Zelda: Ocarina of Time, The</li>
<li class="auto-style2">Major League Baseball featuring Ken Griffey Jr.</li>
<li class="auto-style2">Mario Golf</li>
<li class="auto-style2">New Tetris, The</li>
<li class="auto-style2">Ogre Battle 64: Person of Lordly Caliber</li>
<li class="auto-style2">Pocket Monsters Stadium</li>
<li class="auto-style2">Resident Evil 2</li>
<li class="auto-style2">Super Smash Bros.</li>
<li class="auto-style2">WCW/NWO Revenge</li>
<li class="auto-style2">WWF: Wrestlemania 2000</li>
</ul>

<p class="auto-style2">Animal Crossing (JPN) uses a battery for the real time clock (RTC) chip. </p>

<strong><h3 style="font-family:verdana;">1Mbit <a name="FlashRAM">FlashRAM</a></h3></strong>

<p class="auto-style2">A few games used this rather fancy (and costly) save method.</p>

<ul>
<li class="auto-style2">Command & Conquer</li>
<li class="auto-style2">Jet Force Gemini</li>
<li class="auto-style2">Ken Griffey Jr's Slugfest</li>
<li class="auto-style2">Legend of Zelda: Majora's Mask, The</li>
<li class="auto-style2">Megaman 64</li>
<li class="auto-style2">NBA Courtside 2 featuring Kobe Bryant</li>
<li class="auto-style2">Paper Mario</li>
<li class="auto-style2">Pokemon Puzzle League</li>
<li class="auto-style2">Pokemon Snap</li>
<li class="auto-style2">Pokemon Stadium</li>
<li class="auto-style2">Pokemon Stadium 2</li>
<li class="auto-style2">Starcraft 64</li>
<li class="auto-style2">Tigger's Honey Hunt</li>
<li class="auto-style2">WWF: No Mercy</li>
</ul>
  
<strong><h3 style="font-family:verdana;"><a name="No_Save">No Save</a></h3></strong>

<p class="auto-style2">Surprisingly enough, quite a few N64 games do not save progress at all, not even with a controller pak. We're including these games for the sake of completeness, in case you wondered why some games are not on the above lists. A few of these listed games at least support saving the old fashioned way with passwords.</p>

<ul>
<li class="auto-style2">Batman Beyond: Return of the Joker </li>
	<li class="auto-style2">Batman of the Future - Return of the Joker</li>
<li class="auto-style2">Charlie Blast's Territory (Password)</li>
<li class="auto-style2">Clayfighter 63 1/3 </li>
<li class="auto-style2">Clayfighter: Sculptor's Cut </li>
<li class="auto-style2">Dark Rift </li>
<li class="auto-style2">Elmo's Letter Adventure </li>
<li class="auto-style2">Elmo's Number Journey </li>
<li class="auto-style2">Jeopardy! </li>
<li class="auto-style2">Knife Edge: Nosegunner </li>
<li class="auto-style2">Mace: The Dark Age </li>
<li class="auto-style2">Magical Tetris Challenge </li>
<li class="auto-style2">Monster Truck Madness (Password)</li>
<li class="auto-style2">Mortal Kombat Trilogy </li>
<li class="auto-style2">Powerpuff Girls: Chemical X Traction (Password)</li>
<li class="auto-style2">Rugrats: Scavenger Hunt </li>
<li class="auto-style2">South Park: Chef's Luv Shack </li>
<li class="auto-style2">Transformers Beast Wars: Transmetals</li>
<li class="auto-style2">War Gods </li>
<li class="auto-style2">Wheel of Fortune </li>
</ul>
